      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4360597430418282085">Get Shorty's Chili Palmer is back. No more Mr. Nice Guy. <br />After a smash hit in "Get Leo" and a flop in "Get Lost," B-movie-producer Chili Palmer is looking for another score. Lunching with a record company executive, Chili's exploring a hot new idea--until the exec, a former "associate" from Chili's Brooklyn days, gets whacked while eating his grilled pesto chicken. Lucky C</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4360597430418282085">Get Shorty's Chili Palmer is back. No more Mr. Nice Guy. <br />After a smash hit in "Get Leo" and a flop in "Get Lost," B-movie-producer Chili Palmer is looking for another score. Lunching with a record company executive, Chili's exploring a hot new idea--until the exec, a former "associate" from Chili's Brooklyn days, gets whacked while eating his grilled pesto chicken. Lucky Chili wasn't around for dessert. <br />Segue from real life to reel life. Chili's found his plot. It's a slam-bang opener: the rubout of a record company mogul. Cut to an ambitious wannabe singer named Linda Moon. She has attitude and a band. She's perfect. Zoom into reality. Linda's manager thinks Chili's poaching and he's out to get even, with the help of his switch-hitting Samoan bodyguard. But somebody else beat them to the punch, as Chili discovers when he gets home and finds a corpse at his desk. Somebody made a mistake. . . .</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_657782670">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/657782670" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/51089-jamie" class="left imgcol" title="Jamie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1286573170p2/51089.jpg" alt="Jamie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/657782670?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 03, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/51089-jamie" class="user" title="Jamie">Jamie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/842036.Be_Cool" title="Hardcover 9780385333917" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer657782670">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7126547733973113992">Mr. Chili Palmer says it himself in this one, his own sequel: “A sequel has to be better’n the original or it’s not gonna work.” And I don’t know that it’s better than <em>Shorty</em>, but it’s sure about as much fun.<br /><br />In fact, the only thing denting this one is that in between the two, I watched the movie <em>Get Shorty</em>. Travolta is a love-him-or-hate-him kind of actor, I think, and I lean towards the latter. He was so not the Chili in my mind and I wish I didn't have to work so hard in this one to picture an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7126547733973113992">Mr. Chili Palmer says it himself in this one, his own sequel: “A sequel has to be better’n the original or it’s not gonna work.” And I don’t know that it’s better than <em>Shorty</em>, but it’s sure about as much fun.<br /><br />In fact, the only thing denting this one is that in between the two, I watched the movie <em>Get Shorty</em>. Travolta is a love-him-or-hate-him kind of actor, I think, and I lean towards the latter. He was so not the Chili in my mind and I wish I didn't have to work so hard in this one to picture anyone else but him. In other words, back to the Chili I liked.<br /><br />But that’s all my problem, not the book’s. From the looks of it, I’ll steer clear of the abomination of the movie <em>Be Cool</em>, thank you very much. Which, funny enough, looks to prove the thesis here: once the machine of Hollywood gets its teeth in something, sit back and laugh at how much gets botched. </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130527912" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1366184-jim" class="left imgcol" title="Jim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444092537p2/1366184.jpg" alt="Jim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/130527912?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 14, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1366184-jim" class="user" title="Jim">Jim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1366184-jim?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer130527912">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16195940182312350095">Elmore Leonard pisses me off because he writes so well that, in my nimble mind, the task of writing a novel seems to be a no-brainer. I DO know better. Leonard is so much fun to read because he's so easy to read. That's not to say his writing is simple, far from it. He just does it so well, with a perfect flow to dialogue and exposition. <em>Be Cool</em> is the continued adventures of Chili Palmer and the usual cast of miscreants. Have fun.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1384792497">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16275629811128148894">5 out of 5 <br /><br />For a fun breezy read from the master of the Crime Fiction genre Mr. Elmore Leonard (RIP)<br /><br />Chili ‘look at me’ Palmer, the ex-wise guy (okay so he was ‘loosely connected’) ex-loan shark from Brooklyn by way of Miami Beach, is in Los Angeles now where he has re-invented himself as a movie producer whose in dire need of material for a new film project. And he gets one; at a lunch meeting with a shady record producer which opens the book with a bang.<br /><br />Intrigued by this music business thing, h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16275629811128148894">5 out of 5 <br /><br />For a fun breezy read from the master of the Crime Fiction genre Mr. Elmore Leonard (RIP)<br /><br />Chili ‘look at me’ Palmer, the ex-wise guy (okay so he was ‘loosely connected’) ex-loan shark from Brooklyn by way of Miami Beach, is in Los Angeles now where he has re-invented himself as a movie producer whose in dire need of material for a new film project. And he gets one; at a lunch meeting with a shady record producer which opens the book with a bang.<br /><br />Intrigued by this music business thing, he meets a lovely and talented singer by the name of Linda Moon who wants to be in a band of what she describes as a ‘rock ‘n roll with a twang’ thing, but she can’t follow this dream because she’s currently in another band under contract for a pimp by the name of Raji doing Spice Girls covers (This and many other pop culture touch stones’ like CD’s, MTV music videos, etc. Makes the book feel a bit dated)<br /><br />Soon enough Chili becomes the target of the Russian mob, the pimp and his 250 pound gay Samoan bodyguard by the name of Elliot Wilhelm whom for some reason is in the habit of arching his eyebrows. Amid such hostile environment Chili keeps his cool and wits about him. He’s like a talkative version of a hero in a Sergio Leone Western.<br /><br />This is a fun, breezy read and—as always—Elmore has a way of delivering huge chunks of the plot by way of witty dialog like nobody else in the business. Whenever I’m in need of inspiration in my own ‘literary’ endeavors I always turn to the works of Elmore Leonard for a jolt of inspiration. Which reminds me I should re-read: Tishomingo Blues, City Primeval, Hombre, La Brava…etc., etc., etc.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_29434215">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29434215" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1396160-kandice" class="left imgcol" title="Kandice"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" alt="Kandice" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/29434215?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1396160-kandice" class="user" title="Kandice">Kandice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29434215">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9683277208483148134">I think I like this more because of the reader (Campbell Scott) than the story. When I stop listening and go about my day, I try to think about the plot and what is going on in the tale. It just isn't that great. I get back in the car, turn it on and am immediately sucked in. Scott's voice is just so lovely. It's deep and a bit throaty. He doesn't "do" voices, but somehow you always know when a woman is talking. To me, that's the <strong>real</strong> mark of a great reader.<br /><br />It's a bit unfair to Leonard that I've</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9683277208483148134">I think I like this more because of the reader (Campbell Scott) than the story. When I stop listening and go about my day, I try to think about the plot and what is going on in the tale. It just isn't that great. I get back in the car, turn it on and am immediately sucked in. Scott's voice is just so lovely. It's deep and a bit throaty. He doesn't "do" voices, but somehow you always know when a woman is talking. To me, that's the <strong>real</strong> mark of a great reader.<br /><br />It's a bit unfair to Leonard that I've reviewed his narrator and not his book. This is the sequel to <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_">Get Shorty</a> and is only interesting because Chili Palmer is the star. "Look at me..." I love when Chili says that! I try not to, but I see Chili as Travolta in my mind. The young, thin, beautiful Travolta, like he was in The Boy in the Plastic Bubble, but with a great haircut and clothes. I may drool for a sec here.<br /><br />Anyway, the characters are what make this worth the effort. The plot is sort of lame, but Elaine as Chili's love interest is every bit as interesting as Chili himself. I almost wish Leonard would have gone on to write some Who Dunnits with Chili and Elaine as the Tommy and Tuppence of the series. I'd read those!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9683277208483148134">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/349208681?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10195694-sincere-w" class="user" title="Sincere W.">Sincere W.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer349208681">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer755898586762585604">Jesus, if I'm ever able to write dialogue this well I can die a happy man. <br /><br />This is a fun read, full of interesting characters and very funny scenes. There's Shylocks, gay Samoans, rappers, music execs and a healthy dose of gangsters. The characters develop in unexpected yet logical ways. And the interactions between characters is crisp and authentic.<br /><br />The story concept - if that's what you'd call it - is damn clever, too. The main character, Chili Palmer is putting together what's to be his third</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText755898586762585604">Jesus, if I'm ever able to write dialogue this well I can die a happy man. <br /><br />This is a fun read, full of interesting characters and very funny scenes. There's Shylocks, gay Samoans, rappers, music execs and a healthy dose of gangsters. The characters develop in unexpected yet logical ways. And the interactions between characters is crisp and authentic.<br /><br />The story concept - if that's what you'd call it - is damn clever, too. The main character, Chili Palmer is putting together what's to be his third movie, and this the backbone of the book's plot. Palmer's creative process flows along with the story, so that "actual events" in the book become possible scenes for Palmer's upcoming flick. It made reading the book feel like having a magician explain the trick while he's doing it - and still finding yourself amazed.<br /><br />I haven't read this book's prequel (Get Shorty). But I was never lost or confused; Be Cool stands on it's own. And the small segments of backstory are so well integrated as to be invisible.<br /><br />Great story. Looking forward to reading it again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="755898586762585604">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1438908049">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438908049" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17131437-peter" class="left imgcol" title="Peter"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1360595478p2/17131437.jpg" alt="Peter" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1438908049?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17131437-peter" class="user" title="Peter">Peter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/842036.Be_Cool" title="Hardcover 9780385333917" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17131437-peter?shelf=fiction-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1438908049">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7499860269957515225"><em>Be Cool</em> (1991) is the second in Elmore Leonard’s Chili Palmer series. Ernest (Chili”) Palmer was introduced in <em>Get Shorty</em> as a mob-connected Miami loan shark chasing down a deadbeat in LA. The deadbeat, Harry Zimm, is a producer of B movies and Chili joins with him to produce a movie called <em>Get Leo</em>. The movie is a success and the profits pay off the producer’s loan and give Chili an asset boost. But a sequel named <em>Get Lost</em> tanks at the box office.<br /><br />Chili comes out of it with cash and a reputation</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7499860269957515225"><em>Be Cool</em> (1991) is the second in Elmore Leonard’s Chili Palmer series. Ernest (Chili”) Palmer was introduced in <em>Get Shorty</em> as a mob-connected Miami loan shark chasing down a deadbeat in LA. The deadbeat, Harry Zimm, is a producer of B movies and Chili joins with him to produce a movie called <em>Get Leo</em>. The movie is a success and the profits pay off the producer’s loan and give Chili an asset boost. But a sequel named <em>Get Lost</em> tanks at the box office.<br /><br />Chili comes out of it with cash and a reputation as a movie producer. Now Chili has another movie idea and he meets at a restaurant with Tommy Athens, a record producer, to discuss it. Just as he leaves, a shooter puts a bullet in Tommy’s head. That will undoubtedly be a scene in the movie—as we know from <em>Get Shorty</em>, Chili’s life is so exciting that it becomes the script. Chili’s greatest talent is his mouth. He can talk his way out of, or in to, anything. In <em>Be Cool</em> we watch him do just that.<br /><br />The murder brings Chili into contact with a rich cast of characters: Raji, a record producer and manager of an all-girl band (Odessa, “rock n’ roll with a twang”); Linda Moon, the band’s lead singer; Elliot Wilhelm, a huge Samoan who is Raji’s bodyguard and a movie wannabe; Nick Carcaterre, Raji’s partner; Darryl Holmes, an LA cop and former friend from Miami; Edie Athens, Tommy’s widow and now owner of his record company; Elaine Levin, Chili’s old flame and a film producer at a major studio. Oh, not to forget the Russian mob and Joe Loop, an aging hit man hired by both the Russians and Raji. <br /><br />Chili becomes Linda Moon’s manager, stealing her from Raji who, in turn, sends Joe Loop to kill Chili. But the Russian mob (who had hired Joe to kill Tommy) has also sent a shooter to kill Chili at his house because they think he could connect them to Joe as Tommy’s killer. When Joe walks into Chili’s house to kill him, the Russian is there waiting in the dark for Chili. Mistaking the Russian for Chili, Joe kills the Russian. So now the Russians will double up on Chile, as will Raji. It’s a Keystone Cops of homicide!<br /><br />So we follow Chili around while he’s managing a new singing group, pitching a new movie, evading the Russians and Raji, fending off the vultures roosting on Edie’s recording company, getting a contract for the Linda Moon band, enjoying life with Elaine, and outsmarting everyone. This is a very busy man, but not up to the Chili Palmer of <em>Get Shorty</em>. <br /><br />Three stars.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7499860269957515225">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7399439938712973384">I read a lot of reviews saying this book was way worse than Get Shorty and some of Leonard's worst work but I really enjoyed it. In fact, I think I liked it better than Get Shorty. They are both very similar and I don't see how you could like one and not the other because they're different enough to be different books. I'd give this 3.5 stars if I could, I feel like it was a little better than 3 stars because I enjoyed it so much but not enough to give it 4. Don't let bad reviews fool you, just</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7399439938712973384">I read a lot of reviews saying this book was way worse than Get Shorty and some of Leonard's worst work but I really enjoyed it. In fact, I think I liked it better than Get Shorty. They are both very similar and I don't see how you could like one and not the other because they're different enough to be different books. I'd give this 3.5 stars if I could, I feel like it was a little better than 3 stars because I enjoyed it so much but not enough to give it 4. Don't let bad reviews fool you, just read it and make up your own mind. I'm glad I did</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_26566449">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26566449" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/983898-nekouken" class="left imgcol" title="Nekouken"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Nekouken" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26566449?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 22, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/983898-nekouken" class="user" title="Nekouken">Nekouken</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/842036.Be_Cool" title="Hardcover 9780385333917" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/983898-nekouken?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26566449">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10185183394434874351">Elmore Leonard's <em>Be Cool</em> was the long-awaited sequel to <em>Get Shorty</em>, but as eager as I was to read it, after I was finished, I was not only disappointed but I realized why it was a terrible idea in the first place. In my review of GS, I described Chili Palmer as a neanderthal at a fencing match. In BC, he's the same neanderthal, except he's learned to fence just in time to go bowling. At the time the book starts, Chili is part of the Hollywood machine; his mobby directness is gone in favor of Hol</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10185183394434874351">Elmore Leonard's <em>Be Cool</em> was the long-awaited sequel to <em>Get Shorty</em>, but as eager as I was to read it, after I was finished, I was not only disappointed but I realized why it was a terrible idea in the first place. In my review of GS, I described Chili Palmer as a neanderthal at a fencing match. In BC, he's the same neanderthal, except he's learned to fence just in time to go bowling. At the time the book starts, Chili is part of the Hollywood machine; his mobby directness is gone in favor of Hollywood hemming and hawing, or, more accurately, a simpering hybrid of the two.<br /><br />When he faces a threat on par with the limo guys from GS, he's Chili again, except not nearly as clever and quite tired. When he's dealing with the dating service telemarketer he wants to promote as a music act so he can get a movie idea out of it and finish the three-picture deal that came from the end of the first book, he's compromising everywhere, saying one thing and doing another, and generally behaving like a Hollywood douchebag. <br /><br />This brings me to the reason it was such a bad idea: there's no way Chili could have stayed in Hollywood and become anything but. Chili was an engaging character because he was a fish out of water, but the shift from shylock to movie producer is considerably more drastic than the shift from movie producer to music producer. Perhaps a natural way to make a sequel possible, but the book being something of a satire of sequels itself, it falls as flat as most of its kind. <em>Be Cool</em> follows up an excellent story about conflicting dynamics with a weak one about a multimedia project with attitude.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10185183394434874351">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13994033425016522933">At the Four Seasons...yeah LA not NY, you know I been back a week already. So I'm looking and who comes in but Chili Palmer. Yeah, the man himself. We go back to the old days and he comes over and we catch up. Gives me a Cohiba panatela and we don't light up account of the rules everywhere. And I ask him it bother him the reviews and stuff they say about Be Cool. How they say it don't "measure up" to Get Shorty and "formulaic." And he says, what, he's supposed to read guys who couldn't get somet</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13994033425016522933">At the Four Seasons...yeah LA not NY, you know I been back a week already. So I'm looking and who comes in but Chili Palmer. Yeah, the man himself. We go back to the old days and he comes over and we catch up. Gives me a Cohiba panatela and we don't light up account of the rules everywhere. And I ask him it bother him the reviews and stuff they say about Be Cool. How they say it don't "measure up" to Get Shorty and "formulaic." And he says, what, he's supposed to read guys who couldn't get something reviewed it would save their life. I nod and say fair point but what does he think about it. Being different than feel. He looks at his cigar and wishes for a nice one inch ash and says box office don't write books. And I say truer words, Chil, truer words. So then he says besides, look at Harlequin and all those chick-lit houses. They got rules for their stuff so tight they want it formulaic. I say I get that and was me I'd make 'em all use normal talk like his books. That'd be my rule. He gives me a wink and leaving says send the books and he'll sign. Then I finish my lunch? They tell me it's all taken care of.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38963642">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5386145785306036233">I didn't realize when picking this up (another book sale cheapo) that it was the sequel to Get Shorty, which I don't think I've ever read or seen. (I kept being bothered by the idea of Travolta as Chili Palmer, though that must be the role he plays.) Even as I figured it out, though, I decided to read it anyway. It certainly looked like it could stand on its own.<br /><br />And for the most part, it did. Fast plot, fast characters, fast action, fast read.<br /><br />Which is basically the problem. Even though billed as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5386145785306036233">I didn't realize when picking this up (another book sale cheapo) that it was the sequel to Get Shorty, which I don't think I've ever read or seen. (I kept being bothered by the idea of Travolta as Chili Palmer, though that must be the role he plays.) Even as I figured it out, though, I decided to read it anyway. It certainly looked like it could stand on its own.<br /><br />And for the most part, it did. Fast plot, fast characters, fast action, fast read.<br /><br />Which is basically the problem. Even though billed as the master of contemporary crime fiction, Leonard has no substance in Be Cool. I need to look through my older lists to see what of his I've read -- I seemed to think he was more satire, less face value. But I couldn't find any more than what was on the surface.<br /><br />Blink and you miss it.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7731885338797435050">I liked this book, but I didn't love it as much as other Leonard books. It's set in Hollywood, and although the main character Chili Palmer is out-of-place (having missed both movies, I managed to picture a middle-aged retrosexual and not John Travolta for Chili), the rest of the characters are mostly pretty terrible Hollywood stereotype people. I didn't want to know them better and I didn't care if they succeeded or failed to achieve their superficial desires. Except Eliot: him I loved. Fortuna</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7731885338797435050">I liked this book, but I didn't love it as much as other Leonard books. It's set in Hollywood, and although the main character Chili Palmer is out-of-place (having missed both movies, I managed to picture a middle-aged retrosexual and not John Travolta for Chili), the rest of the characters are mostly pretty terrible Hollywood stereotype people. I didn't want to know them better and I didn't care if they succeeded or failed to achieve their superficial desires. Except Eliot: him I loved. Fortunately, Leonard's talent for writing -- especially for writing dialogue -- kept me engaged even when the plot didn't.<br /><br /></span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1406492011" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16547967-sharon-michael" class="left imgcol" title="Sharon Michael"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Sharon Michael" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1406492011?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16547967-sharon-michael" class="user" title="Sharon Michael">Sharon Michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1406492011">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8153758874082086404">The interesting thing about this book was that the protagonist was a writer who was writing about writing a screenplay. There are different things happening in his life, and he is paying attention to what people say so that he can use their lines as dialogue in a screenplay. So, the reader is being told a story and that story is going to be the basis for another story, which is going to become a movie. All the characters know this, and want to be in the movie.<br /><br />The main character, Chili Palmer, me</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8153758874082086404">The interesting thing about this book was that the protagonist was a writer who was writing about writing a screenplay. There are different things happening in his life, and he is paying attention to what people say so that he can use their lines as dialogue in a screenplay. So, the reader is being told a story and that story is going to be the basis for another story, which is going to become a movie. All the characters know this, and want to be in the movie.<br /><br />The main character, Chili Palmer, meets a woman in Hollywood who wants to become a rock star. He loves the way she talks and wants to make a movie about her. He becomes involved with her agents, and he actually tries to break her contract and become her agent, just to see what happens. The plot thus unfolds, with intrigue, bribes, record companies, movie producers, murder, cops, even Russian gangsters, all very believably woven into the story line.<br /><br />Since the book was written in the nineties, it is a bit outdated, but it was quite insightful with regard to Elmore Leonard’s brilliant method of creating characters, and then letting their dialogue create the story. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8153758874082086404">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1265518573">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1265518573" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/41935777-sam-pendlebury" class="left imgcol" title="Sam Pendlebury"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Sam Pendlebury" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1265518573?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/41935777-sam-pendlebury" class="user" title="Sam Pendlebury">Sam Pendlebury</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1265518573">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2982612450981597276">Chili Palmer, shylock turned producer, back looking for ideas and inspiration for third of three movie deal following success of Get Leo and flop Get Lost. Conceit Elmore Leonard also looking where his fictional character, Chili, will look see where supposedly real life characters take him and these characters themselves alternately wonder if they will play a part in the yet-to-be-written movie or just be used as material for Chili's 'treatment'. Movie was made same title. <br /><br />Hitmen get whacked ego</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2982612450981597276">Chili Palmer, shylock turned producer, back looking for ideas and inspiration for third of three movie deal following success of Get Leo and flop Get Lost. Conceit Elmore Leonard also looking where his fictional character, Chili, will look see where supposedly real life characters take him and these characters themselves alternately wonder if they will play a part in the yet-to-be-written movie or just be used as material for Chili's 'treatment'. Movie was made same title. <br /><br />Hitmen get whacked egos clash dim band members get verbally fxxked with without knowing. Book written with Travolta in mind, felt like he breezes serenely (he is cool) through mayhem and there's a hot part for a female singer <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[but Chili actually gets together with the mature woman, resists the hot singer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Some sections written in expository flashback, we're not there at the time, we only see what we need to. Cameos from Aerosmith, treated with respect, no surprise they're in the movie; Spice Girls disrespected no surprise they're not in it. Leonard sent this book hands-free - could wave his hands in the air he wants to. Terrific book, good too, dialog rings true in a Pulp Fiction Tarantino style. Bit more subtlety most reviewers appear to realise. Leonard makes it effortless. Redundant song sheets don't work for me and the whole music business model seems quaint now. Realism descends quickly into farce. Re-read opening pages you have to.<br /><br />Stephen King cites this book in On Writing so give it a whirl.<br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2982612450981597276">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1472869973" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/50242155-lawstudent-reader" class="left imgcol" title="LawStudent Reader"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450481409p2/50242155.jpg" alt="LawStudent Reader" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1472869973?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/50242155-lawstudent-reader" class="user" title="LawStudent Reader">LawStudent Reader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1472869973">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15924679264024833903">They say the sequel is always the inferior to the original. I didn't think so with this book. Looking back at my review of Get Shorty, I found that my overall thoughts about it were that Leonard was all-tell-and-no-show and that there wasn't enough action. I thought the book had more potential. Be Cool has what Get Shorty was lacking. I enjoyed that there were three plot lines going on at the same time and how Leonard tied them all together at the end in a way that made sense. But what I liked m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15924679264024833903">They say the sequel is always the inferior to the original. I didn't think so with this book. Looking back at my review of Get Shorty, I found that my overall thoughts about it were that Leonard was all-tell-and-no-show and that there wasn't enough action. I thought the book had more potential. Be Cool has what Get Shorty was lacking. I enjoyed that there were three plot lines going on at the same time and how Leonard tied them all together at the end in a way that made sense. But what I liked most of all was the fact that Chili became involved in all of the plot's shenanigans solely for the story. He manipulated things to happen in certain ways because he thought that they would make a good scene in an upcoming movie. It made me wonder if real producers go through life like that - Thinking about the moment from the perspective of viewers instead of living in the moment itself. <br /><br />Stories are only as strong as their main characters and I think I enjoyed this series because I liked Chili. A new kind of gangster, one that instills fear not through violence, but through smooth words and quick thinking. I gave this book 4 stars because sometimes the language dragged and I got characters confused. But overall, it was a more suspenseful read than Get Shorty and I'd recommend those who were iffy about Shorty to read it. Leonard might grow on you.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15924679264024833903">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189471715">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17422959986163625893">I'd put it in 'summer beach read' category. Again Chili P is working on a movie idea and everyone he comes across (and manipulates?) is a potential character or scene. But everything is a scene, no action happens, Chili usually is just describing (talking, talking, talking) to someone what happened. I won't say the ending, but it summed up how I felt about the book - no real story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a href="/review/show/1298687236?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/26895953-ken-doggett" class="user" title="Ken Doggett">Ken Doggett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1298687236">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4207286694791762383">In this one Chili Palmer is a big-time B-movie mogul looking to plot out his next movie with real-life events. At the same time he has to deal with Russian mobsters trying to kill him, along with a local hood and his huge "Samoan" bodyguard trying to do the same. The book actually told me more than I wanted to know about the movie and music business, and even supplied lyrics I didn't need—not sure how, or even if, it contributed to the story. You do have to plow through a lot of seemingly unness</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4207286694791762383">In this one Chili Palmer is a big-time B-movie mogul looking to plot out his next movie with real-life events. At the same time he has to deal with Russian mobsters trying to kill him, along with a local hood and his huge "Samoan" bodyguard trying to do the same. The book actually told me more than I wanted to know about the movie and music business, and even supplied lyrics I didn't need—not sure how, or even if, it contributed to the story. You do have to plow through a lot of seemingly unnessary dialogue, so the book could have been a great deal shorter, but Leonard's talent with dialogue is unsurpassed, and what might have been boring from another writer is often part of the pleasure of this one. The events and masterful plotting kept me reading, and at no time did I want to put the book down and walk away. I rate it at 4 out of 5 stars. Another good one from Leonard!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4207286694791762383">...more</a>

  <a href="/user/show/19589848-pigfender" class="left imgcol" title="Pigfender"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1366410722p2/19589848.jpg" alt="Pigfender" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/831997115?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19589848-pigfender" class="user" title="Pigfender">Pigfender</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14819648-be-cool" title="Paperback 9780753827314" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer831997115">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6445077787817722429">I wanted to like this. People say such good things about Elmore Leonard, and I'd enjoyed the movie version of the first Chili Palmer story (Get Shorty). Sadly, I just can't get on with Leonard's writing. After about 50 pages I muttered something to Mrs Pigfender like "life is too short for books you're not enjoying" and stopped reading. <br /><br />I've tried to put my finger on why I didn't get on with it. My guesses are:<br />- He's trying too hard to be cool and getting it wrong, like a literary version of Guy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6445077787817722429">I wanted to like this. People say such good things about Elmore Leonard, and I'd enjoyed the movie version of the first Chili Palmer story (Get Shorty). Sadly, I just can't get on with Leonard's writing. After about 50 pages I muttered something to Mrs Pigfender like "life is too short for books you're not enjoying" and stopped reading. <br /><br />I've tried to put my finger on why I didn't get on with it. My guesses are:<br />- He's trying too hard to be cool and getting it wrong, like a literary version of Guy Ritchie. Yet his swagger and presumption that you'll love it is so out of place with reality it's like putting Bruce Willis' attitude on Johnny Galecki's body. Don't get me wrong, I like Johnny Galecki. I really do. But he's more believable as Dr Leonard Hofstadter than John McClane. <br />- There is no variation in the pacing. Everything is written in the same relentless speed and tone, which is just plain tiring.<br />- It's so sloppy with the plot. It's just some meandering stroll across the pages while Leonard tries to figure out what to write about. At page 50 there was still no objective (other than for Chili to maybe find a plot for another movie), no lock-in, no antagonist, no urgency, no danger. Sure, someone had ben shot, but Chili didn't care (other than the vague notion that there might be a story in there somewhere) so why should I?<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6445077787817722429">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17766737851216610217">Chili Palmer was a fish-out-of-water, former(?) gangster in the Hollywood business in the book <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_"> Get Shorty</a>. Now he's taking on the music business. Elmore Leonard's dialogue is snappy and I guess the plot evolves in a natural way. But 3/4 through this book, I was ready just to give up. It's a name-dropping, meandering look under the covers at an icky business. Instead of being an interesting fish-out-of-water, Chili ends up just being another uninteresting Hollywood/music industry douchebag - ful</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17766737851216610217">Chili Palmer was a fish-out-of-water, former(?) gangster in the Hollywood business in the book <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_"> Get Shorty</a>. Now he's taking on the music business. Elmore Leonard's dialogue is snappy and I guess the plot evolves in a natural way. But 3/4 through this book, I was ready just to give up. It's a name-dropping, meandering look under the covers at an icky business. Instead of being an interesting fish-out-of-water, Chili ends up just being another uninteresting Hollywood/music industry douchebag - fully invested in, and a part of, the ickyness. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1116810300">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1116810300" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1833765-jason" class="left imgcol" title="Jason"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1391874726p2/1833765.jpg" alt="Jason" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1116810300?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1833765-jason" class="user" title="Jason">Jason</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1116810300">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8807575806199550160">Get Shorty was full of memorable characters and was an engaging read that provided the basis for the hit movie starring John Travolta. Unfortunately, John Travola's portrayal of Chili Palmer seems to have influenced Elmore Leonard's treatment of the character in the sequel, Be Cool. This reads as a movie script and is devoid of the empathetic characters that populated Get Shorty. There are flashes of brilliance throughout the book but they are soon lost to pages and pages of empty dialogue. Mayb</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8807575806199550160">Get Shorty was full of memorable characters and was an engaging read that provided the basis for the hit movie starring John Travolta. Unfortunately, John Travola's portrayal of Chili Palmer seems to have influenced Elmore Leonard's treatment of the character in the sequel, Be Cool. This reads as a movie script and is devoid of the empathetic characters that populated Get Shorty. There are flashes of brilliance throughout the book but they are soon lost to pages and pages of empty dialogue. Maybe the book would be a more engaging read if you wait a while after reading Get Shorty - I read them back to back and feel like I wasted a few days reading this sequel. Stick to your memories of Get Shorty and pretend this sequel was never written. Even for those few moments of brilliance, its just not worth it. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8807575806199550160">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9620228420671064608">Like all of Elmore Leonard's books, this one is full of witty dialogue and quirky characters. Best of all, it is a lot of fun to read. I haven't read Get Shorty, but as much as I liked (and almost never trusted) Chili Palmer, I have added it to my list. I love Leonard's way of delivering chunks of the plot through dialogue.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9620228420671064608">Like all of Elmore Leonard's books, this one is full of witty dialogue and quirky characters. Best of all, it is a lot of fun to read. I haven't read Get Shorty, but as much as I liked (and almost never trusted) Chili Palmer, I have added it to my list. I love Leonard's way of delivering chunks of the plot through dialogue. It takes a great deal of careful talent as a writer to write this way. It also puts us in the hands of the characters as we are taken for a grand ride through their world (which isn't always pretty, but often surprising).<br /><br />This is my third Elmore Leonard book, and it definitely won't be my last.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1109441233">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109441233" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/25528899-kaitlyn-utkewicz" class="left imgcol" title="Kaitlyn Utkewicz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1405049719p2/25528899.jpg" alt="Kaitlyn Utkewicz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1109441233?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/25528899-kaitlyn-utkewicz" class="user" title="Kaitlyn Utkewicz">Kaitlyn Utkewicz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/288973.Be_Cool" title=" 9780141020488" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1109441233">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11051044874129317591">They say the sequel is always the inferior to the original. I didn't think so with this book. Looking back at my review of <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_">Get Shorty</a>, I found that my overall thoughts about it were that Leonard was all-tell-and-no-show and that there wasn't enough action. I thought the book had more potential. Be Cool has what <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_">Get Shorty</a> was lacking. I enjoyed that there were three plot lines going on at the same time and how Leonard tied them all together at the end in a way that made sense. But what I liked m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11051044874129317591">They say the sequel is always the inferior to the original. I didn't think so with this book. Looking back at my review of <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_">Get Shorty</a>, I found that my overall thoughts about it were that Leonard was all-tell-and-no-show and that there wasn't enough action. I thought the book had more potential. Be Cool has what <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_">Get Shorty</a> was lacking. I enjoyed that there were three plot lines going on at the same time and how Leonard tied them all together at the end in a way that made sense. But what I liked most of all was the fact that Chili became involved in all of the plot's shenanigans solely for the story. He manipulated things to happen in certain ways because he thought that they would make a good scene in an upcoming movie. It made me wonder if real producers go through life like that - Thinking about the moment from the perspective of viewers instead of living in the moment itself. <br /><br />Stories are only as strong as their main characters and I think I enjoyed this series because I liked Chili. A new kind of gangster, one that instills fear not through violence, but through smooth words and quick thinking. I gave this book 4 stars because sometimes the language dragged and I got characters confused. But overall, it was a more suspenseful read than <a title="Get Shorty (Chili Palmer, #1) by Elmore Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/702539.Get_Shorty__Chili_Palmer___1_">Get Shorty</a> and I'd recommend those who were iffy about Shorty to read it. Leonard might grow on you. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11051044874129317591">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/722704255?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5880546-rachael-quinn" class="user" title="Rachael Quinn">Rachael Quinn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer722704255">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16941972198867529242">What I love about the Chili Palmer books is how tongue in cheek they are about themselves. It's like watching a really good spoof. In fact, the movie was almost exactly like that, exciting but funny with little asides about not doing cameos. In the first chapter, Chili says that a sequel has to be better than an original. Leonard pulls that off with this book. Actually, the whole book really pokes fun and sequels to the point where all of the people you are supposed to like prefer the first of P</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16941972198867529242">What I love about the Chili Palmer books is how tongue in cheek they are about themselves. It's like watching a really good spoof. In fact, the movie was almost exactly like that, exciting but funny with little asides about not doing cameos. In the first chapter, Chili says that a sequel has to be better than an original. Leonard pulls that off with this book. Actually, the whole book really pokes fun and sequels to the point where all of the people you are supposed to like prefer the first of Palmer's movies, Get Leo, and the bad guys like Get Lost.<br /><br />I forget how I described Get Shorty but I think I called it a riotous rollercoaster ride, or something of the sort. That's exactly how Be Cool is. You have a lot of characters for the length of book and they all play a roll in it somehow, even if it's just a bit part.<br /><br />Palmer calls a dating service one night and has a long conversation with a girl who calls herself Linda Moon. He records the call and starts playing it back to himself, thinking that maybe there is a movie to be made out of it. Linda belongs to a singing group called The Chicks, managed by Raji who has a gay Samoan body guard named Elliot, but what she really wants is for her old band, Odessa, to get back together and to make the record they wanted to make in the first place. When an old acquaintance of Chili's who was in the record business is shot by a Russian wearing a bad rug while they're at lunch, Chili decides it might be time to get into the music business. What follows is a crazy, hilarious romp with people trying to kill Chili and Chili playing people off of each other.<br /><br />I really liked these books. They're not my usual style but I love anything that will get me laughing out loud in public.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16941972198867529242">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_297151705">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297151705" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/930680-elisabeth-crisp" class="left imgcol" title="Elisabeth Crisp"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1324930075p2/930680.jpg" alt="Elisabeth Crisp" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/297151705?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/930680-elisabeth-crisp" class="user" title="Elisabeth Crisp">Elisabeth Crisp</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10973821-be-cool" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer297151705">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2368428245844036864">It's embarrassing to admit that this is the first Elmore Leonard book I've read. Even more embarrassing is that I chose this one because it was available for immediate download from the public library. Look past pragmatism for a moment. Be Cool is more than Chili Palmer #2. It's a send up of the entire genre of movie sequels.<br /><br />Leonard is a master of plot. Protagonist Chili Palmer puts a plan in motion to see what happens next. If it works, the scene stays in the picture. If it doesn't, he'll let t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2368428245844036864">It's embarrassing to admit that this is the first Elmore Leonard book I've read. Even more embarrassing is that I chose this one because it was available for immediate download from the public library. Look past pragmatism for a moment. Be Cool is more than Chili Palmer #2. It's a send up of the entire genre of movie sequels.<br /><br />Leonard is a master of plot. Protagonist Chili Palmer puts a plan in motion to see what happens next. If it works, the scene stays in the picture. If it doesn't, he'll let the screenwriter fix it. He keeps his options open. That's the beauty of Be Cool. The book never steps outside of the box of Hollywood players to examine itself as literature. Yes, it's not as good as Get Shorty or I should say, Get Leo, Chili's fictional first movie. But . . . a sequel never is.<br /><br />Leonard's point of view is so deep that Chili slides easily from retelling scenes to living them, violating the rule of no flashback by essentially becoming an anti-flashback. I love the characters, the music business topicality, and the unexpected violence. Be Cool is labeled crime fiction. Crime farce is a better description.<br /><br />The ending isn't my favorite. It's like an epilogue, tacked on after the essential action is over. Here, Elmore Leonard fails to follow his own advice, to leave out the parts people skip. Maybe, my disappointment has to do with a Kindle edition packed at the end with pages advertising his other works. I wasn't prepared for the story to be over like I would be if I held a printed copy in my hand. Or maybe, Leonard left me dissatisfied on purpose--to leave room for Chili Palmer #3.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2368428245844036864">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_742909659">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742909659" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen Gallup"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321228329p2/1266077.jpg" alt="Stephen Gallup" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/742909659?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="user" title="Stephen Gallup">Stephen Gallup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/842036.Be_Cool" title="Hardcover 9780385333917" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer742909659">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8283841505269212130">Upon finishing <em>Get Shorty</em> recently, I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/731987523">planned</a> to read some more examples of Leonard's writing in the near future. My friend Ed recommended <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183447860">one of his westerns</a>, but as things turned out the next title to come my way was this sequel to Shorty. Just as well. I was still thinking about the way characters in that story were preoccupied with turning their lives into a movie, and <em>Be Cool</em> carries that theme still further.<br /><br />The main character is still Chili Palmer, whose rough life prior to arriving in Hol</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8283841505269212130">Upon finishing <em>Get Shorty</em> recently, I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/731987523">planned</a> to read some more examples of Leonard's writing in the near future. My friend Ed recommended <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183447860">one of his westerns</a>, but as things turned out the next title to come my way was this sequel to Shorty. Just as well. I was still thinking about the way characters in that story were preoccupied with turning their lives into a movie, and <em>Be Cool</em> carries that theme still further.<br /><br />The main character is still Chili Palmer, whose rough life prior to arriving in Hollywood near the beginning of the first book had seemed far removed from the creative realm. I recall how, when he first looked at a screenplay, he didn't know the meaning of terms like INT and POV. So it's almost laughable when on page 5 here he says of screenwriters, "Those guys, most of 'em don't even know where the commas go. You have to rewrite half their stuff." There's no denying Chili does have a rare sense for storytelling, one that perhaps does give him the right to look down his nose at mere screenwriters. Still, the way he has adapted to this new life is almost breathtaking.<br /><br />On the other hand, he remains a very tough guy. His readiness to provoke difficult situations, and his ability to come through them all unscathed, are also remarkable. And that's a large part of how he makes his new career work. Essentially (like any self-respecting novelist), he's constantly looking about for story material. What makes him different is that he engineers events with the explicit intention of trying to <em>create</em> a story in real life that can then be dramatized on film. <br /><br />Along the way, a star is born, people fall in love, and not a few others die violent, spectacular deaths.<br /><br />The detective who is forever picking up the pieces comments, "My wife wants to know how come I'm putting in so much overtime lately. I told her cause Chili Palmer's making a movie."<br /><br />When it's suggested that Chili is tampering with people's lives, he replies, "Yeah, but they're all in character. I'm not making anybody do anything they don't want to."<br /><br />I liked this. Perhaps part of the attraction stems from having written <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.chesfilms.com/what_about_the_boy.htm">a screenplay based on my own life</a>. But perhaps I like it a little less than Shorty. Not sure I can put my finger on the reason, unless it's simply that I have misgivings about whether Chili, that master creator, is himself a convincing character.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8283841505269212130">...more</a>

          </span>

It was first published in hardcover by Doubleday in 1983 and in paperback by the Fawcett Crest imprint of Ballantine Books in 1985.\n\nThe book collects thirty stories by Asimov, most reprinted from magazines and a few previously unpublished, together with a foreword and afterword by the author. Each story is set at a club known as the Union Club, in which a conversation between three members prompts a fourth member, Griswold, to tell about a mystery he has solved. These are often tall stories, and often based on his time in US intelligence. The format is based on that utilized by P. G. Wodehouse in recounting his golf stories.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"13348951067302612395\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));; return false;\"&gt;...more&lt;\/a&gt;\n\n     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12940.Elmore_Leonard">About Elmore Leonard</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/12940.Elmore_Leonard"><img alt="12940" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1240015224p2/12940.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6703405283455672005">Elmore John Leonard lived in Dallas, Oklahoma City and Memphis before settling in Detroit in 1935. After serving in the navy, he studied English literature at the University of Detroit where he entered a short story competition. His earliest published novels in the 1950s were westerns, but Leonard went on to specialize in crime fiction and suspense thrillers, many of which have been adapted into m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6703405283455672005">Elmore John Leonard lived in Dallas, Oklahoma City and Memphis before settling in Detroit in 1935. After serving in the navy, he studied English literature at the University of Detroit where he entered a short story competition. His earliest published novels in the 1950s were westerns, but Leonard went on to specialize in crime fiction and suspense thrillers, many of which have been adapted into motion pictures.<br /><br />Father of <a title="Peter Leonard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/220840.Peter_Leonard">Peter Leonard</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6703405283455672005">...more</a>

    </div>

				<p class="mediumText">No trivia or quizzes yet. <a href="/trivia/work/827574-be-cool">Add some now »</a></p>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/827574-be-cool">Quotes from Be Cool</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“You know what people who go to nude beaches look like?"<br /><br />"Tell me."<br /><br />"People who shouldn't go to nude beaches."<br /><br />"Is Chili Palmer joining the tour?'<br /><br />"I wasn't told"<br /><br />"Ask Nick for me."<br /><br />About a minute went by. Now he heard Nick saying, "Tell him if he goes near Chili Palmer I'll see that he suffers excruciating pain and will never fucking walk again in his life."<br /><br />And, then Robin's voice: "Nick said to tell you that if you go near Chili Palmer he'll have your legs broken."<br /><br />"Why couldn't he say it like that?"<br /><br />"He reads, but the wrong books.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/874805-you-know-what-people-who-go-to-nude-beaches-look" class="actionLinkLite">4 likes</a>
            </nobr>
